      Homer Simpson is also the name of a character in the book
      <a href="/wiki/The_Day_of_the_Locust" title="The Day of the Locust">
       The Day of the Locust
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/The_Day_of_the_Locust_(film)" title="The Day of the Locust (film)">
       film based on the book
      </a>
      .

     <p>
      <b>
       Homer Jay Simpson
      </b>
      is a fictional character in the animated
      <a href="/wiki/Television_program" title="Television program">
       television series
      </a>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons" title="The Simpsons">
        The Simpsons
       </a>
      </i>
      as the patriarch of the
      <a href="/wiki/Simpson_family" title="Simpson family">
       eponymous family
      </a>
      . He is voiced by
      <a href="/wiki/Dan_Castellaneta" title="Dan Castellaneta">
       Dan Castellaneta
      </a>
      and first appeared on television, along with the rest of his family, in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Tracey_Ullman_Show" title="The Tracey Ullman Show">
        The Tracey Ullman Show
       </a>
      </i>
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_shorts" title="The Simpsons shorts">
       short
      </a>
      "
      <a href="/wiki/Good_Night_(The_Simpsons_short)" title="Good Night (The Simpsons short)">
       Good Night
      </a>
      " on April 19, 1987. Homer was created and designed by cartoonist
      <a href="/wiki/Matt_Groening" title="Matt Groening">
       Matt Groening
      </a>
      while he was waiting in the lobby of
      <a href="/wiki/James_L._Brooks" title="James L. Brooks">
       James L. Brooks
      </a>
      ' office. Groening had been called to pitch a series of shorts based on his comic strip
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Life_in_Hell" title="Life in Hell">
        Life in Hell
       </a>
      </i>
      but instead decided to create a new set of characters. He named the character after his father, Homer Groening. After appearing for three seasons on
      <i>
       The Tracey Ullman Show
      </i>
      , the Simpson family got their own series on
      <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">
       Fox
      </a>
      that debuted December 17, 1989.
     </p>
     <p>
      Homer and his wife
      <a href="/wiki/Marge_Simpson" title="Marge Simpson">
       Marge
      </a>
      have three children:
      <a href="/wiki/Bart_Simpson" title="Bart Simpson">
       Bart
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Lisa_Simpson" title="Lisa Simpson">
       Lisa
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Maggie_Simpson" title="Maggie Simpson">
       Maggie
      </a>
      . As the family's provider, he works at the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Springfield_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Springfield Nuclear Power Plant">
       Springfield Nuclear Power Plant
      </a>
      . Homer embodies several American
      <a href="/wiki/Working_class" title="Working class">
       working class
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Stereotype" title="Stereotype">
       stereotypes
      </a>
      : he is crude, bald, overweight, incompetent, clumsy, lazy, a heavy drinker, and ignorant; however, he is essentially a decent man and fiercely devoted to his family. Despite the
      <a href="/wiki/Suburb" title="Suburb">
       suburban
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Blue-collar_worker" title="Blue-collar worker">
       blue-collar
      </a>
      routine of his life, he has had a number of remarkable experiences.
     </p>
     <p>
      In the shorts and earlier episodes, Castellaneta voiced Homer with a loose impression of
      <a href="/wiki/Walter_Matthau" title="Walter Matthau">
       Walter Matthau
      </a>
      ; however, during the second and third seasons of the half-hour show, Homer's voice evolved to become more robust, to allow the expression of a fuller range of emotions. He has appeared in other media relating to
      <i>
       The Simpsons
      </i>
       including video games,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_Movie" title="The Simpsons Movie">
        The Simpsons Movie
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_Ride" title="The Simpsons Ride">
       The Simpsons Ride
      </a>
      , commercials and comic books and inspired an entire line of merchandise. His signature catchphrase, the annoyed grunt "
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/D%27oh!" title="D'oh!">
        D'oh!
       </a>
      </i>
      ", has been included in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Oxford_Dictionary_of_English" title="Oxford Dictionary of English">
        The New Oxford Dictionary of English
       </a>
      </i>
      since 1998 and the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary" title="Oxford English Dictionary">
        Oxford English Dictionary
       </a>
      </i>
      since 2001.
     </p>
     <p>
      Homer is one of the most influential characters in the history of television. The
      <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">
       British
      </a>
      newspaper
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Sunday_Times" title="The Sunday Times">
        The Sunday Times
       </a>
      </i>
      described him as "the greatest comic creation of [modern] time". He was named the greatest character "of the last 20 years" in 2010 by
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">
        Entertainment Weekly
       </a>
      </i>
      , was ranked the second greatest cartoon character by
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/TV_Guide" title="TV Guide">
        TV Guide
       </a>
      </i>
      , behind
      <a href="/wiki/Bugs_Bunny" title="Bugs Bunny">
       Bugs Bunny
      </a>
      , and was voted the greatest television character of all time by
      <a href="/wiki/Channel_4" title="Channel 4">
       Channel 4
      </a>
      viewers. For voicing Homer, Castellaneta has won four
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Awards" title="Primetime Emmy Awards">
       Primetime Emmy Awards
      </a>
      for
      <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Voice-Over_Performance" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Voice-Over Performance">
       Outstanding Voice-Over Performance
      </a>
      and a special-achievement
      <a href="/wiki/Annie_Award" title="Annie Award">
       Annie Award
      </a>
      . In 2000, Homer and his family were awarded a star on the
      <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">
       Hollywood Walk of Fame
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <p>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Role_in_The_Simpsons">
       Role in
       <i>
        The Simpsons
       </i>
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Homer_Simpson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Role in The Simpsons">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Homer is the bumbling husband of Marge and father of Bart, Lisa and Maggie Simpson.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETurner200478.E2.80.9379_1-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETurner200478.E2.80.9379-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He is the son of
      <a href="/wiki/Mona_Simpson_(The_Simpsons)" title="Mona Simpson (The Simpsons)">
       Mona
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Grampa_Simpson" title="Grampa Simpson">
       Abraham Simpson
      </a>
      . Homer held over 188 different jobs in the first 400 episodes of
      <i>
       The Simpsons
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTV_2-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-MTV-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In most episodes, he works as the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuclear_safety" title="Nuclear safety">
       Nuclear Safety
      </a>
      Inspector at the Springfield Nuclear Power Plant, a position he has held since "
      <a href="/wiki/Homer%27s_Odyssey_(The_Simpsons)" title="Homer's Odyssey (The Simpsons)">
       Homer's Odyssey
      </a>
      ", the third episode of the series.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CanWest_3-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-CanWest-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      At the plant, Homer is often ignored and completely forgotten by his boss
      <a href="/wiki/Mr._Burns" title="Mr. Burns">
       Mr. Burns
      </a>
      , and constantly falls asleep and neglects his duties. Matt Groening has stated that he decided to have Homer work at the power plant because of the potential for Homer to wreak havoc.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Each of his other jobs has lasted only one episode. In the first half of the series, the writers developed an explanation about how he got fired from the plant and was then rehired in every episode. In later episodes, he often began a new job on impulse, without any mention of his regular employment.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       The Simpsons
      </i>
      uses a
      <a href="/wiki/Floating_timeline" title="Floating timeline">
       floating timeline
      </a>
      in which the characters
      <a href="/wiki/Ageless" title="Ageless">
       never physically age
      </a>
      , and, as such, the show is generally assumed to be set in the current year. Nevertheless, in several episodes, events in Homer's life have been linked to specific time periods.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETurner200478.E2.80.9379_1-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETurner200478.E2.80.9379-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      "
      <a href="/wiki/Mother_Simpson" title="Mother Simpson">
       Mother Simpson
      </a>
      " (
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_7)" title="The Simpsons (season 7)">
       season seven
      </a>
      , 1995) depicts Homer's mother, Mona, as a radical who went into hiding in 1969 following a run-in with the law;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MotherSimpson_6-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-MotherSimpson-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      "
      <a href="/wiki/The_Way_We_Was" title="The Way We Was">
       The Way We Was
      </a>
      " (
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_2)" title="The Simpsons (season 2)">
       season two
      </a>
      , 1991) shows Homer falling in love with
      <a href="/wiki/Marge_Simpson" title="Marge Simpson">
       Marge Bouvier
      </a>
      as a senior at Springfield High School in 1974;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WayWeWas_7-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WayWeWas-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and "
      <a href="/wiki/I_Married_Marge" title="I Married Marge">
       I Married Marge
      </a>
      " (
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_3)" title="The Simpsons (season 3)">
       season three
      </a>
      , 1991) implies that Marge became pregnant with Bart in 1980.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMarriedMarge_8-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-IMarriedMarge-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, the episode "
      <a href="/wiki/That_%2790s_Show" title="That '90s Show">
       That '90s Show
      </a>
      " (
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_19)" title="The Simpsons (season 19)">
       season 19
      </a>
      , 2008) contradicted much of this backstory, portraying Homer and Marge as a childless couple in the early 1990s.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Homer's age has changed as the series developed; he was 36 in the early episodes,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beauty_10-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Beauty-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      38 and 39 in
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_8)" title="The Simpsons (season 8)">
       season eight
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and 40 in the
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_18)" title="The Simpsons (season 18)">
       eighteenth season
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      although even in those seasons his age is inconsistent.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETurner200478.E2.80.9379_1-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETurner200478.E2.80.9379-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      During
      <a href="/wiki/Bill_Oakley" title="Bill Oakley">
       Bill Oakley
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Josh_Weinstein" title="Josh Weinstein">
       Josh Weinstein
      </a>
      's period as showrunners, they found that as they aged, Homer seemed to become older too, so they increased his age to 38.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Character">
       Character
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Homer_Simpson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Character">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Creation">
       Creation
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Homer_Simpson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Creation">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Naming the characters after members of his own family, Homer was named after Groening's father Homer Groening, who himself had been named after ancient Greek poet
      <a href="/wiki/Homer" title="Homer">
       Homer
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-americasfirstfamily_14-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-americasfirstfamily-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Very little else of Homer's character was based on him, and to prove that the meaning behind Homer's name was not significant, Groening later named his own son Homer.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to Groening, "Homer originated with my goal to both amuse my real father, and just annoy him a little bit. My father was an athletic, creative, intelligent filmmaker and writer, and the only thing he had in common with Homer was a love of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Donut" title="Donut">
       donuts
      </a>
      ."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW_2010_19-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-EW_2010-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Although Groening has stated in several interviews that Homer was named after his father, he also claimed in several 1990 interviews that a character in the 1939
      <a href="/wiki/Nathanael_West" title="Nathanael West">
       Nathanael West
      </a>
      novel
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Day_of_the_Locust" title="The Day of the Locust">
        The Day of the Locust
       </a>
      </i>
      was the inspiration for naming Homer.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETurner200478.E2.80.9379_1-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETurner200478.E2.80.9379-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Homer's middle initial "J", which stands for "Jay",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      is a "tribute" to animated characters such as
      <a href="/wiki/Bullwinkle_J._Moose" title="Bullwinkle J. Moose">
       Bullwinkle J. Moose
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Rocky_the_Flying_Squirrel" title="Rocky the Flying Squirrel">
       Rocket J. Squirrel
      </a>
      from
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Rocky_and_Bullwinkle_Show" title="The Rocky and Bullwinkle Show">
        The Rocky and Bullwinkle Show
       </a>
      </i>
      , who got their middle initial from
      <a href="/wiki/Jay_Ward" title="Jay Ward">
       Jay Ward
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Homer made his debut with the rest of the Simpson family on April 19, 1987, in
      <i>
       The Tracey Ullman Show
      </i>
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_shorts" title="The Simpsons shorts">
       short
      </a>
      "
      <a href="/wiki/Good_Night_(The_Simpsons_short)" title="Good Night (The Simpsons short)">
       Good Night
      </a>
      ".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERichmond_.26_Coffman199714_25-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERichmond_.26_Coffman199714-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 1989, the shorts were adapted into
      <i>
       The Simpsons
      </i>
      , a half-hour series airing on the
      <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">
       Fox Broadcasting Company
      </a>
      . Homer and the Simpson family remained the main characters on this new show.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Design">
       Design
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Homer_Simpson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Design">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Evolution_of_Homer.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="201" data-file-width="370" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fd/Evolution_of_Homer.jpg/250px-Evolution_of_Homer.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/f/fd/Evolution_of_Homer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/f/fd/Evolution_of_Homer.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Evolution_of_Homer.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Homer's design has been revised several times over the course of the series. Left to right: Homer as he appeared in "
        <a href="/wiki/Good_Night_(The_Simpsons_short)" title="Good Night (The Simpsons short)">
         Good Night
        </a>
        " (1987), "
        <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_shorts" title="The Simpsons shorts">
         Bathtime
        </a>
        " (1989), and "
        <a href="/wiki/Bart_the_Genius" title="Bart the Genius">
         Bart the Genius
        </a>
        " (1990).
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The entire Simpson family was designed so that they would be recognizable in silhouette.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The family was crudely drawn because Groening had submitted basic sketches to the animators, assuming they would clean them up; instead, they just traced over his drawings.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-americasfirstfamily_14-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-americasfirstfamily-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Homer's physical features are generally not used in other characters; for example, in the later seasons, no characters other than Homer,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lenny_Leonard" title="Lenny Leonard">
       Lenny
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Krusty_the_Clown" title="Krusty the Clown">
       Krusty the Clown
      </a>
      have a similar beard line.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
       <a href="#cite_note-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      When Groening originally designed Homer, he put his initials into the character's hairline and ear: the hairline resembled an 'M', and the right ear resembled a 'G'. Groening decided that this would be too distracting and redesigned the ear to look normal. However, he still draws the ear as a 'G' when he draws pictures of Homer for fans.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The basic shape of Homer's head is described by director
      <a href="/wiki/Mark_Kirkland" title="Mark Kirkland">
       Mark Kirkland
      </a>
      as a tube-shaped coffee can with a salad bowl on top. Bart's head is also coffee-can shaped, while spheres are used for Marge, Lisa, and Maggie.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      During the shorts, the animators experimented with the way Homer would move his mouth when talking. At one point, his mouth would stretch out back "beyond his beardline"; but this was dropped when it got "out of control."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
       <a href="#cite_note-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In some early episodes, Homer's hair was rounded rather than sharply pointed because animation director
      <a href="/wiki/Wes_Archer" title="Wes Archer">
       Wes Archer
      </a>
      felt it should look disheveled. Homer's hair evolved to be consistently pointed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dancin_32-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Dancin-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      During the first three seasons, Homer's design for some close-up shots included small lines which were meant to be eyebrows. Matt Groening strongly disliked them and they were eventually dropped.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dancin_32-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Dancin-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_7)" title="The Simpsons (season 7)">
       season seven
      </a>
      (1995) episode "
      <a href="/wiki/Treehouse_of_Horror_VI" title="Treehouse of Horror VI">
       Treehouse of Horror VI
      </a>
      ", Homer was computer animated into a
      <a href="/wiki/3D_computer_graphics" title="3D computer graphics">
       three-dimensional
      </a>
      character for the first time for the "Homer
      <sup>
       3
      </sup>
      " segment of the episode. The computer animation directors at
      <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Data_Images" title="Pacific Data Images">
       Pacific Data Images
      </a>
      worked hard not to "reinvent the character".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3D_33-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-3D-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the final minute of the segment, the 3D Homer ends up in a real world, live-action
      <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">
       Los Angeles
      </a>
      . The scene was directed by
      <a href="/wiki/David_Mirkin" title="David Mirkin">
       David Mirkin
      </a>
      and was the first time a
      <i>
       Simpsons
      </i>
      character had been in the real world in the series.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3D_33-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-3D-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Because "
      <a href="/wiki/Lisa%27s_Wedding" title="Lisa's Wedding">
       Lisa's Wedding
      </a>
      " (
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_6)" title="The Simpsons (season 6)">
       season six
      </a>
      , 1995) is set fifteen years in the future, Homer's design was altered to make him older in the episode. He is heavier; one of the hairs on top of his head was removed; and an extra line was placed under the eye. A similar design has been used in subsequent
      <a href="/wiki/Flashforward" title="Flashforward">
       flashforwards
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
       <a href="#cite_note-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Voice">
       Voice
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Homer_Simpson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Voice">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dan_Castellaneta_2.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="468" data-file-width="533" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Dan_Castellaneta_2.jpg/200px-Dan_Castellaneta_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Dan_Castellaneta_2.jpg/300px-Dan_Castellaneta_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Dan_Castellaneta_2.jpg/400px-Dan_Castellaneta_2.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dan_Castellaneta_2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        "I was trying to find something I was more comfortable with that had more power to it, so I had to drop the voice down. [...] People will say to me, 'Boy, I'm glad they replaced the guy that was there that first season.' That was me!"
        <div style="text-align:right;">
         
         <a href="/wiki/Dan_Castellaneta" title="Dan Castellaneta">
          Dan Castellaneta
         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FN_35-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FN-35">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           35
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Homer's voice is performed by
      <a href="/wiki/Dan_Castellaneta" title="Dan Castellaneta">
       Dan Castellaneta
      </a>
      , who voices numerous other characters, including
      <a href="/wiki/Grampa_Simpson" title="Grampa Simpson">
       Grampa Simpson
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Krusty_the_Clown" title="Krusty the Clown">
       Krusty the Clown
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Barney_Gumble" title="Barney Gumble">
       Barney Gumble
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Groundskeeper_Willie" title="Groundskeeper Willie">
       Groundskeeper Willie
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Mayor_Quimby" title="Mayor Quimby">
       Mayor Quimby
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Hans_Moleman" title="Hans Moleman">
       Hans Moleman
      </a>
      . Castellaneta had been part of the regular cast of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Tracey_Ullman_Show" title="The Tracey Ullman Show">
        The Tracey Ullman Show
       </a>
      </i>
      and had previously done some voice-over work in
      <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">
       Chicago
      </a>
      alongside his wife
      <a href="/wiki/Deb_Lacusta" title="Deb Lacusta">
       Deb Lacusta
      </a>
      . Voices were needed for the
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_shorts" title="The Simpsons shorts">
       Simpsons shorts
      </a>
      , so the producers decided to ask Castellaneta and fellow cast member
      <a href="/wiki/Julie_Kavner" title="Julie Kavner">
       Julie Kavner
      </a>
      to voice Homer and Marge rather than hire more actors.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FN_35-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-FN-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Age_36-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-The_Age-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the shorts and first few seasons of the half-hour show, Homer's voice is different from the majority of the series. The voice began as a loose impression of
      <a href="/wiki/Walter_Matthau" title="Walter Matthau">
       Walter Matthau
      </a>
      , but Castellaneta could not "get enough power behind that voice",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Age_36-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-The_Age-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and could not sustain his Matthau impression for the nine- to ten-hour-long recording sessions and had to find something easier.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTV_2-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-MTV-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      During the second and third seasons of the half-hour show, Castellaneta "dropped the voice down"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FN_35-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-FN-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and developed it as more versatile and humorous, allowing Homer a fuller range of emotions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-matthau_37-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-matthau-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Castellaneta's normal speaking voice has no similarity to Homer's.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aspen_38-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Aspen-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      To perform Homer's voice, Castellaneta lowers his chin to his chest
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Age_36-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-The_Age-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and is said to "let his I.Q. go".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mirkin_39-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Mirkin-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      While in this state, he has ad-libbed several of Homer's least intelligent comments,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mirkin_39-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Mirkin-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      such as the line "I am so smart, s-m-r-t" from "
      <a href="/wiki/Homer_Goes_to_College" title="Homer Goes to College">
       Homer Goes to College
      </a>
      " (
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_5)" title="The Simpsons (season 5)">
       season five
      </a>
      , 1993) which was a genuine mistake made by Castellaneta during recording.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CastellanetaBIC_40-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-CastellanetaBIC-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Castellaneta likes to stay in character during recording sessions,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tribune_41-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Tribune-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and he tries to visualize a scene so that he can give the proper voice to it.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
       <a href="#cite_note-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Despite Homer's fame, Castellaneta claims he is rarely recognized in public, "except, maybe, by a die-hard fan".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tribune_41-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Tribune-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      "
      <a href="/wiki/Homer%27s_Barbershop_Quartet" title="Homer's Barbershop Quartet">
       Homer's Barbershop Quartet
      </a>
      " (
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_5)" title="The Simpsons (season 5)">
       season five
      </a>
      , 1993) is the only episode where Homer's voice was provided by someone other than Castellaneta. The episode features Homer forming a
      <a href="/wiki/Barbershop_music" title="Barbershop music">
       barbershop quartet
      </a>
      called The Be Sharps; and, at some points, his singing voice is provided by a member of
      <a href="/wiki/The_Dapper_Dans" title="The Dapper Dans">
       The Dapper Dans
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERichmond_.26_Coffman1997120_43-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERichmond_.26_Coffman1997120-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Dapper Dans had recorded the singing parts for all four members of The Be Sharps. Their singing was intermixed with the normal voice actor's voices, often with a regular voice actor singing the melody and the Dapper Dans providing backup.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
       <a href="#cite_note-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Until 1998, Castellaneta was paid $30,000 per episode. During a pay dispute in 1998, Fox threatened to replace the six main voice actors with new actors, going as far as preparing for casting of new voices.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Glaister_45-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Glaister-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, the dispute was soon resolved and he received $125,000 per episode until 2004 when the voice actors demanded that they be paid $360,000 an episode.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Glaister_45-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Glaister-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The issue was resolved a month later,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
       <a href="#cite_note-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and Castellaneta earned $250,000 per episode.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
       <a href="#cite_note-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      After salary re-negotiations in 2008, the voice actors receive approximately $400,000 per episode.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
       <a href="#cite_note-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Three years later, with Fox threatening to cancel the series unless production costs were cut, Castellaneta and the other cast members accepted a 30 percent pay cut, down to just over $300,000 per episode.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
       <a href="#cite_note-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Character_development">
       Character development
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Homer_Simpson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Character development">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Executive producer
      <a href="/wiki/Al_Jean" title="Al Jean">
       Al Jean
      </a>
      notes that in
      <i>
       The Simpsons
      </i>
      ' writing room, "everyone loves writing for Homer", and many of his adventures are based on experiences of the writers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the early seasons of the show, Bart was the main focus. But, around the
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_4)" title="The Simpsons (season 4)">
       fourth season
      </a>
      , Homer became more of the focus. According to Matt Groening, this was because "With Homer, there's just a wider range of jokes you can do. And there are far more drastic consequences to Homer's stupidity. There's only so far you can go with a juvenile delinquent. We wanted Bart to do anything up to the point of him being tried in court as an adult. But Homer is an adult, and his boneheaded-ness is funnier. [...] Homer is launching himself headfirst into every single impulsive thought that occurs to him."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW_2010_19-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-EW_2010-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Homer's behavior has changed a number of times through the run of the series. He was originally "very angry" and oppressive toward Bart, but these characteristics were toned down somewhat as his persona was further explored.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In early seasons, Homer appeared concerned that his family was going to make him look bad; however, in later episodes he was less anxious about how he was perceived by others.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disgrace_52-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-disgrace-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the first several years, Homer was often portrayed as sweet and sincere, but during
      <a href="/wiki/Mike_Scully" title="Mike Scully">
       Mike Scully
      </a>
      's tenure as executive producer (
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_9)" title="The Simpsons (season 9)">
       seasons nine
      </a>
      , 1997 to
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_12)" title="The Simpsons (season 12)">
       twelve
      </a>
      , 2001), he became more of "a boorish, self-aggrandizing oaf".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
       <a href="#cite_note-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Chris Suellentrop of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Slate_(magazine)" title="Slate (magazine)">
        Slate
       </a>
      </i>
      wrote, "under Scully's tenure, The Simpsons became, well, a cartoon. [...] Episodes that once would have ended with
      <a href="/wiki/Duffless" title="Duffless">
       Homer and Marge bicycling into the sunset
      </a>
      [...] now end with
      <a href="/wiki/It%27s_a_Mad,_Mad,_Mad,_Mad_Marge" title="It's a Mad, Mad, Mad, Mad Marge">
       Homer blowing a tranquilizer dart into Marge's neck
      </a>
      ."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
       <a href="#cite_note-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Fans have dubbed this incarnation of the character "Jerkass Homer".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
       <a href="#cite_note-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Back_56-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Back-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
       <a href="#cite_note-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      At voice recording sessions, Dan Castellaneta has rejected material written in the script that portrayed Homer as being too mean. He believes that Homer is "boorish and unthinking, but he'd never be mean on purpose."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SundayTimes_58-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-SundayTimes-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      When editing
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_Movie" title="The Simpsons Movie">
        The Simpsons Movie
       </a>
      </i>
      , several scenes were changed or otherwise toned down to make Homer more sympathetic.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_59-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-com-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The writers have made Homer's intelligence appear to decline over the years; they explain this was not done intentionally, but it was necessary to top previous jokes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138th_60-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-138th-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      For example, in "
      <a href="/wiki/When_You_Dish_Upon_a_Star" title="When You Dish Upon a Star">
       When You Dish Upon a Star
      </a>
      ", (
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_10)" title="The Simpsons (season 10)">
       season 10
      </a>
      , 1998) the writers included a scene where Homer admits that he cannot read. The writers debated including this plot twist because it would contradict previous scenes in which Homer does read, but eventually they decided to keep the joke because they found it humorous. The writers often debate how far to go in portraying Homer's stupidity; one suggested rule is that "he can never forget his own name".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dish_61-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Dish-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Personality">
       Personality
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Homer_Simpson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Personality">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The comic efficacy of Homer's personality lies in his frequent bouts of bumbling stupidity and laziness, and his explosive anger. He has a low intelligence level and is described by director
      <a href="/wiki/David_Silverman_(animator)" title="David Silverman (animator)">
       David Silverman
      </a>
      as "creatively brilliant in his stupidity".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sundvd_62-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-sundvd-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Homer also shows immense apathy towards work, is overweight, and "is devoted to his stomach".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sundvd_62-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-sundvd-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      His short attention span is evidenced by his impulsive decisions to engage in various hobbies and enterprises, only to "change ... his mind when things go badly".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sundvd_62-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-sundvd-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Homer often spends his evenings drinking
      <a href="/wiki/Duff_Beer" title="Duff Beer">
       Duff Beer
      </a>
      at
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moe%27s_Tavern" title="Moe's Tavern">
       Moe's Tavern
      </a>
      , and was shown in the episode "
      <a href="/wiki/Duffless" title="Duffless">
       Duffless
      </a>
      " (
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_4)" title="The Simpsons (season 4)">
       season four
      </a>
      , 1993) as a full-blown
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcoholic" title="Alcoholic">
       alcoholic
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
       <a href="#cite_note-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He is very envious of his neighbors,
      <a href="/wiki/Ned_Flanders" title="Ned Flanders">
       Ned Flanders
      </a>
      and his family, and is easily enraged by
      <a href="/wiki/Bart_Simpson" title="Bart Simpson">
       Bart
      </a>
      . Homer will often strangle Bart on impulse in a cartoonish manner. The first instance of Homer strangling Bart was in the short "Family Portrait". According to Matt Groening, the rule was that Homer could only strangle Bart impulsively, never with pre-meditation,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
       <a href="#cite_note-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      because doing so "seems sadistic. If we keep it that he's ruled by his impulses, then he can easily switch impulses. So, even though he impulsively wants to strangle Bart, he also gives up fairly easily."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW_2010_19-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-EW_2010-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Another of the original ideas entertained by Groening was that Homer would "always get his comeuppance or Bart had to strangle him back", but this was dropped.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
       <a href="#cite_note-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Homer shows no compunction about expressing his rage, and does not attempt to hide his actions from people outside the family.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sundvd_62-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-sundvd-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HomerStranglesBart.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="343" data-file-width="434" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/93/HomerStranglesBart.jpg/200px-HomerStranglesBart.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/93/HomerStranglesBart.jpg/300px-HomerStranglesBart.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/93/HomerStranglesBart.jpg/400px-HomerStranglesBart.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HomerStranglesBart.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The first sketch of Homer strangling Bart, drawn in 1988.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Homer has complex relationships with all three of his children, and the rest of his family. He often berates Bart, but the two commonly share adventures and are sometimes allies; some episodes, particularly in later seasons, show that the pair have a strange respect for each other's cunning. Homer and Lisa have opposite personalities and he usually overlooks Lisa's talents, but when made aware of his neglect, does everything he can to help her. While Homer's thoughtless antics often upset his family, he has also revealed himself to be a caring father and husband: in "
      <a href="/wiki/Lisa_the_Beauty_Queen" title="Lisa the Beauty Queen">
       Lisa the Beauty Queen
      </a>
      ", (
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_4)" title="The Simpsons (season 4)">
       season four
      </a>
      , 1992) he sold his cherished ride on the Duff blimp and used the money to enter Lisa in a beauty pageant so she could feel better about herself;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beauty_10-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Beauty-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      in "
      <a href="/wiki/Rosebud_(The_Simpsons)" title="Rosebud (The Simpsons)">
       Rosebud
      </a>
      ", (
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_5)" title="The Simpsons (season 5)">
       season five
      </a>
      , 1993) he gave up his chance at wealth to allow Maggie to keep a cherished teddy bear, despite the show also occasionally implying Homer forgets he has a third child, while the episode "
      <a href="/wiki/And_Maggie_Makes_Three" title="And Maggie Makes Three">
       And Maggie Makes Three
      </a>
      " suggests she is the chief reason Homer took and remains at his regular job (
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_6)" title="The Simpsons (season 6)">
       season six
      </a>
      , 1995);
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
       <a href="#cite_note-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      in "
      <a href="/wiki/Radio_Bart" title="Radio Bart">
       Radio Bart
      </a>
      ", (
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_3)" title="The Simpsons (season 3)">
       season three
      </a>
      , 1992) he spearheaded an attempt to dig Bart out after he had fallen down a well;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and in "
      <a href="/wiki/A_Milhouse_Divided" title="A Milhouse Divided">
       A Milhouse Divided
      </a>
      ", (
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_8)" title="The Simpsons (season 8)">
       season eight
      </a>
      , 1996) he arranged a surprise second wedding with Marge to make up for their unsatisfactory first ceremony.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
       <a href="#cite_note-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Homer, however, has a poor relationship with his father
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abraham_Simpson" title="Abraham Simpson">
       Abraham "Grampa" Simpson
      </a>
      , whom he placed in a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nursing_home" title="Nursing home">
       nursing home
      </a>
      as soon as he could.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
       <a href="#cite_note-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Simpson family will often do their best to avoid unnecessary contact with Grampa, but Homer has shown feelings of love for his father from time to time.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
       <a href="#cite_note-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Homer is "a (happy) slave to his various appetites",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETurner200483_71-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETurner200483-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and would gladly
      <a href="/wiki/Treehouse_of_Horror_IV#The_Devil_and_Homer_Simpson" title="Treehouse of Horror IV">
       sell his soul to the devil in exchange for a single doughnut
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He has an apparently vacuous mind but at times exhibits a surprising depth of knowledge about various subjects, such as the composition of the
      <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">
       Supreme Court of the United States
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Incan_mythology" title="Incan mythology">
       Incan mythology
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bankruptcy_law" title="Bankruptcy law">
       bankruptcy law
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Cell_biology" title="Cell biology">
       cell biology
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Homer's brief periods of intelligence are overshadowed, however, by much longer and consistent periods of ignorance, forgetfulness, and stupidity. Homer has a low
      <a href="/wiki/Intelligence_quotient" title="Intelligence quotient">
       IQ
      </a>
      of 55 which has variously been attributed to the hereditary "Simpson Gene" (which eventually causes every male member of the family to become incredibly stupid),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      his alcohol problem, exposure to radioactive waste, repetitive cranial trauma,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
       <a href="#cite_note-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and a crayon lodged in the
      <a href="/wiki/Frontal_lobe" title="Frontal lobe">
       frontal lobe
      </a>
      of his brain.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HOMR_79-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HOMR-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the episode "
      <a href="/wiki/HOMR" title="HOMR">
       HOMR
      </a>
      " (
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_12)" title="The Simpsons (season 12)">
       season 12
      </a>
      , 2001) Homer gets surgery to remove the (newly discovered) crayon from his brain, boosting his IQ to 105, but although he bonds very well with Lisa, his newfound capacity for understanding and reason makes him less happy and he gets
      <a href="/wiki/Moe_Szyslak" title="Moe Szyslak">
       Moe
      </a>
      to reinsert a crayon, causing his intelligence to return to its previous level.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HOMR_79-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HOMR-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Homer often debates with his own mind, which is expressed in voiceover. His brain has a record of giving him dubious advice, sometimes helping him make the right decisions, but often failing spectacularly. It has even become completely frustrated and, through sound effects, walked out on him,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Homer's conversations with his brain were used several times during the fourth season, but were later phased out after the producers "used every possible permutation".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Duffless_81-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Duffless-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      These exchanges were often introduced because they filled time and were easy for the animators to work on.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Duffless_81-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Duffless-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">
       Reception
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Homer_Simpson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Reception">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Commendations">
       Commendations
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Homer_Simpson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Commendations">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Simpsons_star.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2504" data-file-width="2912" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/The_Simpsons_star.jpg/200px-The_Simpsons_star.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/The_Simpsons_star.jpg/300px-The_Simpsons_star.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/The_Simpsons_star.jpg/400px-The_Simpsons_star.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Simpsons_star.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        In 2000, Homer, along with the rest of the Simpson family, was awarded a star on the Hollywood Walk of Fame.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_The_Simpsons" title="List of awards and nominations received by The Simpsons">
       List of awards and nominations received by The Simpsons
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Homer's influence on comedy and culture has been significant. In 2010,
      <i>
       Entertainment Weekly
      </i>
      named Homer "the greatest character of the last 20 years."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He was placed second on
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/TV_Guide" title="TV Guide">
        TV Guide
       </a>
      </i>
      's 2002 Top 50 Greatest Cartoon Characters, behind
      <a href="/wiki/Bugs_Bunny" title="Bugs Bunny">
       Bugs Bunny
      </a>
      ;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bugs_83-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Bugs-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      fifth on
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bravo_(U.S._TV_channel)" title="Bravo (U.S. TV channel)">
       Bravo's
      </a>
      100 Greatest TV Characters, one of only four cartoon characters on that list;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
       <a href="#cite_note-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and first in a
      <a href="/wiki/Channel_4" title="Channel 4">
       Channel 4
      </a>
      poll of the greatest television characters of all time.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2007,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">
        Entertainment Weekly
       </a>
      </i>
      placed Homer ninth on their list of the "50 Greatest TV icons" and first on their 2010 list of the "Top 100 Characters of the Past Twenty Years".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
       <a href="#cite_note-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20years_87-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-20years-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20years2_88-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-20years2-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Homer was also the runaway winner in British polls that determined who viewers thought was the "greatest American"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and which fictional character people would like to see become the
      <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">
       President of the United States
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      His relationship with Marge was included in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/TV_Guide" title="TV Guide">
        TV Guide
       </a>
      </i>
      's list of "The Best TV Couples of All Time".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Dan Castellaneta has won several awards for voicing Homer, including four
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Awards" title="Primetime Emmy Awards">
       Primetime Emmy Awards
      </a>
      for "
      <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Voice-Over_Performance" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Voice-Over Performance">
       Outstanding Voice-Over Performance
      </a>
      " in 1992 for "
      <a href="/wiki/Lisa%27s_Pony" title="Lisa's Pony">
       Lisa's Pony
      </a>
      ", 1993 for "
      <a href="/wiki/Mr._Plow" title="Mr. Plow">
       Mr. Plow
      </a>
      ",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Emmys_92-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Emmys-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      in 2004 for "
      <a href="/wiki/Today_I_Am_a_Clown" title="Today I Am a Clown">
       Today I Am a Clown
      </a>
      ",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schneider_93-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Schneider-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and in 2009 for "
      <a href="/wiki/Father_Knows_Worst" title="Father Knows Worst">
       Father Knows Worst
      </a>
      ".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
       <a href="#cite_note-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Although in the case of "Today I Am a Clown", it was for voicing "various characters" and not solely for Homer.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schneider_93-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Schneider-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In
      <a href="/wiki/62nd_Primetime_Emmy_Awards" title="62nd Primetime Emmy Awards">
       2010
      </a>
      , Castellaneta received a fifth Emmy nomination for voicing Homer and Grampa in the episode "
      <a href="/wiki/Thursdays_with_Abie" title="Thursdays with Abie">
       Thursdays with Abie
      </a>
      ".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
       <a href="#cite_note-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 1993, Castellaneta was given a special
      <a href="/wiki/Annie_Award" title="Annie Award">
       Annie Award
      </a>
      , "Outstanding Individual Achievement in the Field of Animation", for his work as Homer on
      <i>
       The Simpsons
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
       <a href="#cite_note-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
       <a href="#cite_note-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2004, Castellaneta and
      <a href="/wiki/Julie_Kavner" title="Julie Kavner">
       Julie Kavner
      </a>
      (the voice of Marge) won a
      <a href="/wiki/Young_Artist_Award" title="Young Artist Award">
       Young Artist Award
      </a>
      for "Most Popular Mom &amp; Dad in a TV Series".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-YAA_98-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-YAA-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        98
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2005, Homer and Marge were nominated for a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teen_Choice_Award" title="Teen Choice Award">
       Teen Choice Award
      </a>
      for "Choice TV Parental Units".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
       <a href="#cite_note-99">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        99
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Various episodes in which Homer is strongly featured have won Emmy Awards for
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Animated_Program_(for_Programming_Less_Than_One_Hour)" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Animated Program (for Programming Less Than One Hour)">
       Outstanding Animated Program
      </a>
      , including "
      <a href="/wiki/Homer_vs._Lisa_and_the_8th_Commandment" title="Homer vs. Lisa and the 8th Commandment">
       Homer vs. Lisa and the 8th Commandment
      </a>
      " in 1991, "
      <a href="/wiki/Lisa%27s_Wedding" title="Lisa's Wedding">
       Lisa's Wedding
      </a>
      " in 1995, "
      <a href="/wiki/Homer%27s_Phobia" title="Homer's Phobia">
       Homer's Phobia
      </a>
      " in 1997, "
      <a href="/wiki/Trash_of_the_Titans" title="Trash of the Titans">
       Trash of the Titans
      </a>
      " in 1998, "
      <a href="/wiki/HOMR" title="HOMR">
       HOMR
      </a>
      " in 2001, "
      <a href="/wiki/Three_Gays_of_the_Condo" title="Three Gays of the Condo">
       Three Gays of the Condo
      </a>
      " in 2003 and "
      <a href="/wiki/Eternal_Moonshine_of_the_Simpson_Mind" title="Eternal Moonshine of the Simpson Mind">
       Eternal Moonshine of the Simpson Mind
      </a>
      " in 2008.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Emmys_92-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Emmys-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2000, Homer and the rest of the Simpson family were awarded a star on the
      <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">
       Hollywood Walk of Fame
      </a>
      located at 7021 Hollywood Boulevard.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
       <a href="#cite_note-100">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        100
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Analysis">
       Analysis
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Homer_Simpson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Analysis">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Homer is an "
      <a href="/wiki/Everyman" title="Everyman">
       everyman
      </a>
      " and embodies several American stereotypes of working class
      <a href="/wiki/Blue-collar_worker" title="Blue-collar worker">
       blue-collar
      </a>
      men: he is crude, overweight, incompetent, dim witted, clumsy and a borderline alcoholic.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETurner200478.E2.80.9379_1-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETurner200478.E2.80.9379-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Matt Groening describes him as "completely ruled by his impulses".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
       <a href="#cite_note-101">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        101
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Dan Castellaneta calls him "a dog trapped in a man's body", adding, "He's incredibly loyal not entirely clean but you gotta love him."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Age_36-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-The_Age-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In his book
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Planet_Simpson" title="Planet Simpson">
        Planet Simpson
       </a>
      </i>
      , author
      <a href="/wiki/Chris_Turner_(author)" title="Chris Turner (author)">
       Chris Turner
      </a>
      describes Homer as "the most American of the Simpsons" and believes that while the other Simpson family members could be changed to other nationalities, Homer is "pure American".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETurner200480_102-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETurner200480-102">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        102
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the book
      <i>
       God in the Details: American Religion in Popular Culture
      </i>
      , the authors comment that "Homer's progress (or lack thereof) reveals a character who can do the right thing, if accidentally or begrudgingly."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
       <a href="#cite_note-103">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        103
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The book
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_and_Philosophy:_The_D%27oh!_of_Homer" title="The Simpsons and Philosophy: The D'oh! of Homer">
        The Simpsons and Philosophy: The D'oh! of Homer
       </a>
      </i>
      includes a chapter analyzing Homer's character from the perspective of
      <a href="/wiki/Aristotelianism" title="Aristotelianism">
       Aristotelian
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Virtue_ethics" title="Virtue ethics">
       virtue ethics
      </a>
      . Raja Halwani writes that Homer's "love of life" is an admirable character trait, "for many people are tempted to see in Homer nothing but buffoonery and immorality. [...] He is not politically correct, he is more than happy to judge others, and he certainly does not seem to be obsessed with his health. These qualities might not make Homer an admirable
      <i>
       person
      </i>
      , but they do make him admirable in some ways, and, more importantly, makes us crave him and the Homer Simpsons of this world."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
       <a href="#cite_note-104">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        104
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2008,
      <i>
       Entertainment Weekly
      </i>
      justified designating
      <i>
       The Simpsons
      </i>
      as a television classic by stating, "we all hail Simpson patriarch Homer because his joy is as palpable as his stupidity is stunning".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
       <a href="#cite_note-105">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        105
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_8)" title="The Simpsons (season 8)">
       season eight
      </a>
      episode "
      <a href="/wiki/Homer%27s_Enemy" title="Homer's Enemy">
       Homer's Enemy
      </a>
      " the writers decided to examine "what it would be like to actually work alongside Homer Simpson".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
       <a href="#cite_note-106">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        106
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The episode explores the possibilities of a realistic character with a strong
      <a href="/wiki/Work_ethic" title="Work ethic">
       work ethic
      </a>
      named Frank Grimes placed alongside Homer in a work environment. In the episode, Homer is portrayed as an everyman and the embodiment of the American spirit; however, in some scenes his negative characteristics and silliness are prominently highlighted.
