      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETurner200499.E2.80.93106_107-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETurner200499.E2.80.93106-107">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        107
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
       <a href="#cite_note-108">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        108
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      By the end of the episode, Grimes, a hard working and persevering "real American hero", has become the villain; the viewer is intended to be pleased that Homer has emerged victorious.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETurner200499.E2.80.93106_107-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETurner200499.E2.80.93106-107">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        107
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In
      <i>
       Gilligan Unbound
      </i>
      , author
      <a href="/wiki/Paul_Cantor" title="Paul Cantor">
       Paul Arthur Cantor
      </a>
      states that he believes Homer's devotion to his family has added to the popularity of the character. He writes, "Homer is the distillation of pure fatherhood. [...] This is why, for all his stupidity, bigotry and self-centered quality, we cannot hate Homer. He continually fails at being a good father, but he never gives up trying, and in some basic and important sense that makes him a good father."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
       <a href="#cite_note-109">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        109
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Sunday_Times" title="The Sunday Times">
        The Sunday Times
       </a>
      </i>
      remarked "Homer is good because, above all, he is capable of great love. When the chips are down, he always does the right thing by his childrenhe is never unfaithful in spite of several opportunities."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SundayTimes_58-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-SundayTimes-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_influence">
       Cultural influence
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Homer_Simpson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Cultural influence">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Homer Simpson is one of the most popular and influential television characters in a variety of standards.
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">
        USA Today
       </a>
      </i>
      cited the character as being one of the "top 25 most influential people of the past 25 years" in 2007, adding that Homer "epitomized the irony and irreverence at the core of American humor."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
       <a href="#cite_note-110">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        110
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Robert_Thompson_(media_scholar)" title="Robert Thompson (media scholar)">
       Robert Thompson
      </a>
      , director of
      <a href="/wiki/Syracuse_University" title="Syracuse University">
       Syracuse University
      </a>
      's Center for the Study of Popular Television believes that "three centuries from now, English professors are going to be regarding Homer Simpson as one of the greatest creations in human storytelling."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
       <a href="#cite_note-111">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        111
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Animation historian
      <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Beck" title="Jerry Beck">
       Jerry Beck
      </a>
      described Homer as one of the best animated characters, saying, "you know someone like it, or you identify with (it). That's really the key to a classic character."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bugs_83-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Bugs-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Homer has been described by
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Sunday_Times" title="The Sunday Times">
        The Sunday Times
       </a>
      </i>
      as "the greatest comic creation of [modern] time". The article remarked, "every age needs its great, consoling failure, its lovable, pretension-free mediocrity. And we have ours in Homer Simpson."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SundayTimes_58-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-SundayTimes-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Homer has been cited as a bad influence on children; for example, in 2005 a survey conducted in the
      <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
       United Kingdom
      </a>
      found that 59% of parents felt that Homer promoted an unhealthy lifestyle.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
       <a href="#cite_note-112">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        112
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A five-year study of more than 2,000 middle-aged people in
      <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
       France
      </a>
      found a possible link between weight and brain function, the findings of which were dubbed the "Homer Simpson syndrome".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hss_113-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-hss-113">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        113
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Results from a word memory test showed that people with a
      <a href="/wiki/Body_mass_index" title="Body mass index">
       Body mass index
      </a>
      (BMI) of 20 (considered to be a healthy level) remembered an average of nine out of 16 words. Meanwhile, people with a BMI of 30 (inside the obese range) remembered an average of just seven out of 16 words.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hss_113-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-hss-113">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        113
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Despite Homer's embodiment of
      <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_States" title="Culture of the United States">
       American culture
      </a>
      , his influence has spread to other parts of the world. In 2003, Matt Groening revealed that his father, after whom Homer was named, was
      <a href="/wiki/Canadians" title="Canadians">
       Canadian
      </a>
      , and said that this made Homer himself a Canadian.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
       <a href="#cite_note-114">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        114
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The character was later made an
      <a href="/wiki/Honorary_citizenship" title="Honorary citizenship">
       honorary citizen
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg" title="Winnipeg">
       Winnipeg
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">
       Canada
      </a>
      , in
      <a href="/wiki/Real_life" title="Real life">
       real life
      </a>
      because Homer Groening was believed to be from the
      <a href="/wiki/Manitoba" title="Manitoba">
       Manitoba
      </a>
      capital, although sources say the senior Groening was actually born in
      <a href="/wiki/Saskatchewan" title="Saskatchewan">
       Saskatchewan
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
       <a href="#cite_note-115">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        115
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2007, an image of Homer was painted next to the
      <a href="/wiki/Cerne_Abbas_Giant" title="Cerne Abbas Giant">
       Cerne Abbas Giant
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Dorset" title="Dorset">
       Dorset
      </a>
      , England as part of a promotion for
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_Movie" title="The Simpsons Movie">
        The Simpsons Movie
       </a>
      </i>
      . This caused outrage among local
      <a href="/wiki/Modern_paganism" title="Modern paganism">
       neopagans
      </a>
      who performed "
      <a href="/wiki/Rainmaking_(ritual)" title="Rainmaking (ritual)">
       rain magic
      </a>
      " to try to get it washed away.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
       <a href="#cite_note-116">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        116
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2008, a fake
      <a href="/wiki/Spanish_euro_coins" title="Spanish euro coins">
       Spanish euro
      </a>
      coin was found in
      <a href="/wiki/Avil%C3%A9s" title="Avils">
       Avils
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
       Spain
      </a>
      with the face of Homer replacing the effigy of
      <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Spain" title="Monarchy of Spain">
       King
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Juan_Carlos_I_of_Spain" title="Juan Carlos I of Spain">
       Juan Carlos I
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
       <a href="#cite_note-117">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        117
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On April 9, 2009, the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Postal_Service" title="United States Postal Service">
       United States Postal Service
      </a>
      unveiled a series of five 44 cent stamps featuring Homer and the four other members of the Simpson family. They are the first characters from a television series to receive this recognition while the show is still in production.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
       <a href="#cite_note-118">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        118
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The stamps, designed by Matt Groening, were made available for purchase on May 7, 2009.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
       <a href="#cite_note-119">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        119
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
       <a href="#cite_note-120">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        120
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Homer has appeared, voiced by Castellaneta, in several other television shows, including the
      <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_6)" title="American Idol (season 6)">
       sixth season
      </a>
      of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">
        American Idol
       </a>
      </i>
      where he opened the show;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
       <a href="#cite_note-121">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        121
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Tonight_Show_with_Jay_Leno" title="The Tonight Show with Jay Leno">
        The Tonight Show with Jay Leno
       </a>
      </i>
      where he performed a special animated opening monologue for the July 24, 2007, edition;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
       <a href="#cite_note-122">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        122
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the 2008
      <a href="/wiki/Fundraising" title="Fundraising">
       fundraising
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Television_special" title="Television special">
       television special
      </a>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Stand_Up_to_Cancer" title="Stand Up to Cancer">
        Stand Up to Cancer
       </a>
      </i>
      where he was shown having a
      <a href="/wiki/Colonoscopy" title="Colonoscopy">
       colonoscopy
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
       <a href="#cite_note-123">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        123
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="D.27oh.21">
       D'oh!
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Homer_Simpson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: D'oh!">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/D%27oh!" title="D'oh!">
       D'oh!
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Homer's catchphrase, the annoyed grunt "D'oh!", is typically uttered when he injures himself, realizes that he has done something stupid, or when something bad has happened or is about to happen to him. During the voice recording session for a
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Tracey_Ullman_Show" title="The Tracey Ullman Show">
        Tracey Ullman Show
       </a>
      </i>
      short, Homer was required to utter what was written in the script as an "annoyed grunt". Dan Castellaneta rendered it as a drawn out "d'ooooooh". This was inspired by
      <a href="/wiki/James_Finlayson_(actor)" title="James Finlayson (actor)">
       Jimmy Finlayson
      </a>
      , the mustachioed Scottish actor who appeared in 33
      <a href="/wiki/Laurel_and_Hardy" title="Laurel and Hardy">
       Laurel and Hardy
      </a>
      films. Finlayson had used the term as a
      <a href="/wiki/Minced_oath" title="Minced oath">
       minced oath
      </a>
      to stand in for the word "
      <a href="/wiki/Damnation" title="Damnation">
       Damn
      </a>
      !"
      <a href="/wiki/Matt_Groening" title="Matt Groening">
       Matt Groening
      </a>
      felt that it would better suit the timing of animation if it were spoken faster. Castellaneta then shortened it to a quickly uttered "D'oh!"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-herald_124-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-herald-124">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        124
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The first intentional use of D'oh! occurred in the Ullman short "The Krusty the Clown Show"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-herald_124-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-herald-124">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        124
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      (1989), and its first usage in the series was in the series premiere, "
      <a href="/wiki/Simpsons_Roasting_on_an_Open_Fire" title="Simpsons Roasting on an Open Fire">
       Simpsons Roasting on an Open Fire
      </a>
      ".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-doh_125-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-doh-125">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        125
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      "D'oh!" was first added to
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Oxford_Dictionary_of_English" title="Oxford Dictionary of English">
        The New Oxford Dictionary of English
       </a>
      </i>
      in 1998. It is defined as an
      <a href="/wiki/Interjection" title="Interjection">
       interjection
      </a>
      "used to comment on an action perceived as foolish or stupid".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
       <a href="#cite_note-126">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        126
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2001, "D'oh!" was added to the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary" title="Oxford English Dictionary">
        Oxford English Dictionary
       </a>
      </i>
      , without the apostrophe ("Doh!").
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
       <a href="#cite_note-127">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        127
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The definition of the word is "expressing frustration at the realization that things have turned out badly or not as planned, or that one has just said or done something foolish".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
       <a href="#cite_note-128">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        128
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2006, "D'oh!" was placed in sixth position on
      <a href="/wiki/TV_Land" title="TV Land">
       TV Land
      </a>
      's list of the 100 greatest television catchphrases.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
       <a href="#cite_note-129">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        129
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">
       <a href="#cite_note-130">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        130
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      "D'oh!" is also included in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Oxford_Dictionary_of_Quotations" title="The Oxford Dictionary of Quotations">
        The Oxford Dictionary of Quotations
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">
       <a href="#cite_note-131">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        131
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The book includes several other quotations from Homer, including "Kids, you tried your best and you failed miserably. The lesson is never try", from "
      <a href="/wiki/Burns%27_Heir" title="Burns' Heir">
       Burns' Heir
      </a>
      " (
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_5)" title="The Simpsons (season 5)">
       season five
      </a>
      , 1994) as well as "Kids are the best, Apu. You can teach them to hate the things you hate. And they practically raise themselves, what with the Internet and all", from "
      <a href="/wiki/Eight_Misbehavin%27" title="Eight Misbehavin'">
       Eight Misbehavin'
      </a>
      " (
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_11)" title="The Simpsons (season 11)">
       season 11
      </a>
      , 1999). Both quotes entered the dictionary in August 2007.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">
       <a href="#cite_note-132">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        132
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Merchandising">
       Merchandising
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Homer_Simpson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Merchandising">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Homer's inclusion in many Simpsons publications, toys, and other merchandise is evidence of his enduring popularity.
      <i>
       The Homer Book
      </i>
      , about Homer's personality and attributes, was released in 2004 and is commercially available.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">
       <a href="#cite_note-133">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        133
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_134-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-CNN-134">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        134
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It has been described as "an entertaining little book for occasional reading"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">
       <a href="#cite_note-135">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        135
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and was listed as one of "the most interesting books of 2004" by
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Chattanoogan" title="The Chattanoogan">
        The Chattanoogan
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">
       <a href="#cite_note-136">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        136
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Other merchandise includes dolls, posters, figurines,
      <a href="/wiki/Bobblehead" title="Bobblehead">
       bobblehead dolls
      </a>
      , mugs, alarm clocks, jigsaw puzzles,
      <a href="/wiki/Chia_Pet" title="Chia Pet">
       Chia Pets
      </a>
      , and clothing such as slippers, T-shirts, baseball caps, and boxer shorts.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
       <a href="#cite_note-137">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        137
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Homer has appeared in commercials for
      <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">
       Coke
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/MCI_Communications" title="MCI Communications">
       1-800-COLLECT
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Burger_King" title="Burger King">
       Burger King
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Butterfinger" title="Butterfinger">
       Butterfinger
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/C.C._Lemon" title="C.C. Lemon">
       C.C. Lemon
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Church%27s_Chicken" title="Church's Chicken">
       Church's Chicken
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Domino%27s_Pizza" title="Domino's Pizza">
       Domino's Pizza
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">
       Intel
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/KFC" title="KFC">
       Kentucky Fried Chicken
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ramada" title="Ramada">
       Ramada Inn
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Subway_(restaurant)" title="Subway (restaurant)">
       Subway
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/T.G.I._Friday%27s" title="T.G.I. Friday's">
       T.G.I. Friday's
      </a>
      . In 2004, Homer starred in a
      <a href="/wiki/MasterCard" title="MasterCard">
       MasterCard
      </a>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/MasterCard#Advertising" title="MasterCard">
        Priceless
       </a>
      </i>
      commercial that aired during
      <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXXVIII" title="Super Bowl XXXVIII">
       Super Bowl XXXVIII
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">
       <a href="#cite_note-138">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        138
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2001,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kellogg_Company" title="Kellogg Company">
       Kelloggs
      </a>
      launched a brand of cereal called "Homer's Cinnamon Donut Cereal", which was available for a limited time.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_134-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-CNN-134">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        134
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">
       <a href="#cite_note-139">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        139
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In June 2009, Dutch
      <a href="/wiki/Automotive_navigation_system" title="Automotive navigation system">
       automotive navigation systems
      </a>
      manufacturer
      <a href="/wiki/TomTom" title="TomTom">
       TomTom
      </a>
      announced that Homer would be added to its downloadable
      <a href="/wiki/Global_Positioning_System" title="Global Positioning System">
       GPS
      </a>
      voice lineup. Homer's voice, recorded by Dan Castellaneta, features several in-character comments such as "Take the third right. We might find an ice cream truck! Mmm... ice cream."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">
       <a href="#cite_note-140">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        140
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Homer has appeared in other media relating to
      <i>
       The Simpsons
      </i>
      . He has appeared in every one of
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_The_Simpsons_video_games" title="List of The Simpsons video games">
       <i>
        The Simpsons
       </i>
       video games
      </a>
      , including the most recent,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_Game" title="The Simpsons Game">
        The Simpsons Game
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">
       <a href="#cite_note-141">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        141
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Alongside the television series, Homer regularly appears in issues of
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_The_Simpsons_comics" title="List of The Simpsons comics">
       <i>
        Simpsons Comics
       </i>
      </a>
      , which were first published on November 29, 1993, and are still issued monthly.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gazette_142-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-gazette-142">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        142
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msnbc_143-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-msnbc-143">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        143
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Homer also plays a role in
      <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_Ride" title="The Simpsons Ride">
       The Simpsons Ride
      </a>
      , launched in 2008 at
      <a href="/wiki/Universal_Studios_Florida" title="Universal Studios Florida">
       Universal Studios Florida
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Universal_Studios_Hollywood" title="Universal Studios Hollywood">
       Hollywood
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">
       <a href="#cite_note-144">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        144
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
